				<div class="minerva__subtitle"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=MetLife_Inc.&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="MetLife Inc.">MetLife Inc.</a>)</span></div>
			</div>
			
			<div id="bodyContent" class="content"><div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="mw-parser-output"><section class="mf-section-0" id="mf-section-0"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Metropolitan Life" redirects here. For the book by Fran Lebowitz, see <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Life_(book)" title="Metropolitan Life (book)">Metropolitan Life (book)</a>.</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For the <i>League of Legends</i> player formerly known as Matlife, see <a href="/wiki/Matt_Elento" class="mw-redirect" title="Matt Elento">Matt Elento</a>.</div>
<p><b>MetLife, Inc.</b> is the <a href="/wiki/Holding_company" title="Holding company">holding corporation</a> for the <b>Metropolitan Life Insurance Company</b> (<b>MLIC</b>),<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> better known as <b>MetLife</b>, and its affiliates. MetLife is among the largest global providers of <a href="/wiki/Insurance" title="Insurance">insurance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Annuity_(US_financial_products)" class="mw-redirect" title="Annuity (US financial products)">annuities</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Employee_benefit" class="mw-redirect" title="Employee benefit">employee benefit</a> programs, with 90 million customers in over 60 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-NintyMillion_10_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NintyMillion_10-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BWIRE_09_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BWIRE_09-4">[4]</a></sup> The firm was founded on March 24, 1868.<sup id="cite_ref-GBook_06_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GBook_06-5">[5]</a></sup> MetLife ranked No. 43 in the 2018 <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> list of the largest United States corporations by total revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p><table class="infobox rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.metlife.com/">MetLife.com</a></td></tr></tbody></table><p>On January 6, 1915, MetLife completed the <a href="/wiki/Mutualization" title="Mutualization">mutualization</a> process, changing from a stock life insurance company owned by individuals to a <a href="/wiki/Mutual_organization" title="Mutual organization">mutual company</a> operating without external shareholders and for the benefit of policyholders.<sup id="cite_ref-Mutualzation_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mutualzation-7">[7]</a></sup> After 85 years as a mutual company, MetLife <a href="/wiki/Demutualization" title="Demutualization">demutualized</a> into a <a href="/wiki/Public_company" title="Public company">publicly traded company</a> with an <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">initial public offering</a> in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-IPO_Deal_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IPO_Deal-8">[8]</a></sup> Through its subsidiaries and affiliates, MetLife holds leading market positions in the United States, Japan, Latin America, Asia's Pacific region, Europe, and the Middle East.<sup id="cite_ref-AlicoInternational_10_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AlicoInternational_10-9">[9]</a></sup> MetLife serves 90 of the largest <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> companies.<sup id="cite_ref-Ninety_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ninety-10">[10]</a></sup></p><p>The company's principal offices are located at <a href="/wiki/MetLife_Building" title="MetLife Building">200 Park Avenue, New York City</a> in <a href="/wiki/Midtown_Manhattan" title="Midtown Manhattan">Midtown Manhattan</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, though it retains some executive offices and its boardroom in the <a href="/wiki/MetLife_Building" title="MetLife Building">MetLife Building</a>, located at 200 Park Avenue, New York City, which it sold in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_05_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_05-11">[11]</a></sup></p><p>In January 2016, the company announced that it would spin off its U.S. retail business, including individual life insurance and annuities for the retail market, in a separate company called <a href="/wiki/Brighthouse_Financial" title="Brighthouse Financial">Brighthouse Financial</a>, which launched in March 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> The continuing MetLife company kept naming rights to <a href="/wiki/MetLife_Stadium" title="MetLife Stadium">MetLife Stadium</a> in northern <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none"><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(1)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_structure">Corporate structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MetLife&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Corporate structure" data-section="1" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-1 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-1">
<table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">December 2015</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table><p>As of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MetLife&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the company was "organized into five segments: Insurance Products, Retirement Products," the US Business (including Auto &amp; Home and Corporate Benefit Funding), and International.<sup id="cite_ref-Disability10K_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Disability10K-14">[14]</a></sup>  The Insurance Products division was the largest unit, accounting for 53% of 2009 revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-MexEng_103_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MexEng_103-15">[15]</a></sup>  By 2015, a division referred to as "Americas" had emerged.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_governance">Corporate governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MetLife&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Corporate governance" data-section="2" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<table class="box-Expand_section plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MetLife&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">December 2015</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table><p>As of May 2019, MetLife's <a href="/wiki/Chief_executive_officer" title="Chief executive officer">chief executive officer</a> was Michel A. Khalaf and its non-executive chairman of the board was <a href="/wiki/Glenn_Hubbard_(economist)" title="Glenn Hubbard (economist)">Glenn Hubbard</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p><p>In 2015, MetLife hired Hugh Dineen to fill the new role of <a href="/wiki/Chief_marketing_officer" title="Chief marketing officer">chief marketing officer</a> within the US Business Unit.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p><p>As in many large, public corporations, MetLife has a <a href="/wiki/Compensation_committee" class="mw-redirect" title="Compensation committee">compensation committee</a> which establishes compensation levels for the company's senior executives; MetLife compensation emphasizes "variable performance-based compensation over fixed or guaranteed pay".<sup id="cite_ref-:0_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Subsidiary_and_affiliate_companies">Subsidiary and affiliate companies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MetLife&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Subsidiary and affiliate companies" data-section="3" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>MetLife subsidiaries and affiliates have included MetLife Investors, MetLife Bank, MetLife Securities, Metropolitan Property and Casualty Insurance Company and its subsidiaries, General American, Hyatt Legal, MetLife Resources, New England Financial, Walnut Street Securities, Inc., Safeguard Health Enterprises, Inc., and Tower Square Securities, Inc., Cigna.<sup id="cite_ref-HyattLegal_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HyattLegal-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MetLifeInvestorsTwo_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MetLifeInvestorsTwo-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MetLifeBankHistory_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MetLifeBankHistory-21">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Securities_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Securities-22">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Fortune_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fortune-23">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Conneticut_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Conneticut-24">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GeneralAmerican_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GeneralAmerican-25">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Safeguard_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Safeguard-26">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Three_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Three-27">[27]</a></sup></p><p>The subsidiary MetLife Insurance Company USA, as of 2015 headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Charlotte,_North_Carolina" title="Charlotte, North Carolina">Charlotte, North Carolina</a>, was formerly known as MetLife Insurance Company of Connecticut, and prior to this as <a href="/wiki/Travelers_Insurance_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Travelers Insurance Company">Travelers Insurance Company</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p><p>MetLife Bank was sold to <a href="/wiki/GE_Capital" title="GE Capital">GE Capital</a> in 2013, and MetLife exited the banking business.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p><p>Metlife in partnership with <a href="/wiki/Tishman_Realty_%26_Construction" title="Tishman Realty &amp; Construction">Tishman Realty &amp; Construction</a> co-owns the <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_World" title="Walt Disney World">Walt Disney World</a> <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_World_Swan" title="Walt Disney World Swan">Swan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_World_Dolphin" title="Walt Disney World Dolphin">Dolphin</a> resort in <a href="/wiki/Lake_Buena_Vista,_Florida" title="Lake Buena Vista, Florida">Lake Buena Vista, Florida</a>. The land on which the hotels are located on is owned by <a href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Company" title="The Walt Disney Company">The Walt Disney Company</a> and is leased to Metlife and Tishman (which owns the buildings) and operated by <a href="/wiki/Starwood" title="Starwood">Starwood Hotels &amp; Resorts</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Westin_Hotels_%26_Resorts" title="Westin Hotels &amp; Resorts">Westin</a> hotel.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(2)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MetLife&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: History" data-section="4" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-2 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-2">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years">Early years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MetLife&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Early years" data-section="5" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tichnor_Brothers_New_England_Mutual_Life_front.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Tichnor_Brothers_New_England_Mutual_Life_front.jpg/220px-Tichnor_Brothers_New_England_Mutual_Life_front.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="551" data-file-height="355"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 142px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Tichnor_Brothers_New_England_Mutual_Life_front.jpg/220px-Tichnor_Brothers_New_England_Mutual_Life_front.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="142" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tichnor_Brothers_New_England_Mutual_Life_front.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Home office of the New England Mutual Life Insurance Co. one of the predecessor companies of MetLife. see <sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>The predecessor company to MetLife began in 1863 when a group of <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> businessmen raised $100,000 to found the <b>National Union Life and Limb Insurance Company</b>. The company insured <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">Civil War</a> sailors and soldiers against disabilities due to wartime wounds, accidents, and sickness. On March 24, 1868, it became known as Metropolitan Life Insurance Company and shifted its focus to the life insurance business.<sup id="cite_ref-Book_06_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Book_06-33">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Origin_10_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Origin_10-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Metropolitan_Life_Insurance_Company_Tower_at_Night_with_Fog.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Metropolitan_Life_Insurance_Company_Tower_at_Night_with_Fog.jpg/220px-Metropolitan_Life_Insurance_Company_Tower_at_Night_with_Fog.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="1024"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 293px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Metropolitan_Life_Insurance_Company_Tower_at_Night_with_Fog.jpg/220px-Metropolitan_Life_Insurance_Company_Tower_at_Night_with_Fog.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="293" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Metropolitan_Life_Insurance_Company_Tower_at_Night_with_Fog.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Life_Insurance_Company_Tower" title="Metropolitan Life Insurance Company Tower">Metropolitan Life Insurance Company Tower</a>, which previously served as company headquarters, was featured in its advertising for many years.</div></div></div>
<p>A severe business depression that began with the <a href="/wiki/Panic_of_1873" title="Panic of 1873">Panic of 1873</a> forced the company to contract, until it reached its lowest point in the late 1870s.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> After observing the insurance industry in Great Britain in 1879, MetLife President Joseph F. Knapp brought “industrial” or “workingmen’s” insurance programs to the United States – insurance issued in small amounts on which premiums were collected weekly or monthly at the policyholder's home. By 1880, sales had exceeded a quarter million of such policies, resulting in nearly $1 million in revenue from premiums. In 1909, MetLife had become the nation's largest life insurer in the United States, as measured by life insurance in force (the total value of life insurance policies issued).<sup id="cite_ref-Book_06_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Book_06-33">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Networth_01_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Networth_01-35">[35]</a></sup></p><p>In 1890, the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Life_Insurance_Company_Tower" title="Metropolitan Life Insurance Company Tower">Metropolitan Life Insurance Company Building</a> was commissioned to serve as MetLife's home office on 23rd Street in Manhattan. The building was completed in stages through 1905. A clock tower was commissioned adjacent to the home office in 1907, and when completed two years later, the building was the world's tallest until 1913.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> The home office complex, which came to include the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Life_North_Building" title="Metropolitan Life North Building">Metropolitan Life North Building</a> remained the company's headquarters until 2005. For many years, an illustration of the Metropolitan Life clock tower (with light emanating from the tip of its spire and the slogan, "The Light That Never Fails") featured prominently in MetLife's <a href="/wiki/Advertising" title="Advertising">advertising</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Building_05_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Building_05-37">[37]</a></sup></p><p>By 1930, MetLife insured one of five men, women, and children in the United States and <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-History_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History-38">[38]</a></sup> During the 1930s, it also began to diversify its portfolio by reducing the percentage of individual mortgages in favor of public utility bonds, investments in government securities, and loans for commercial real estate.<sup id="cite_ref-History_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History-38">[38]</a></sup> The company financed the construction of the <a href="/wiki/Empire_State_Building" title="Empire State Building">Empire State Building</a> in 1929 as well as provided capital to build <a href="/wiki/Rockefeller_Center" title="Rockefeller Center">Rockefeller Center</a> in 1931. During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, MetLife placed more than 51 percent of its total assets in war bonds, and was the largest single private contributor to the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied</a> cause.<sup id="cite_ref-History_38-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Postwar">Postwar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MetLife&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Postwar" data-section="6" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leroy_Lincoln_Metropolitan_Life.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Leroy_Lincoln_Metropolitan_Life.jpg/220px-Leroy_Lincoln_Metropolitan_Life.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="624" data-file-height="471"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 166px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Leroy_Lincoln_Metropolitan_Life.jpg/220px-Leroy_Lincoln_Metropolitan_Life.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="166" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leroy_Lincoln_Metropolitan_Life.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Company president Leroy Lincoln in 1947</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Metlife_1970.png" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e2/Metlife_1970.png/180px-Metlife_1970.png" decoding="async" width="180" height="35" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="310" data-file-height="61"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 180px;height: 35px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e2/Metlife_1970.png/180px-Metlife_1970.png" data-alt="" data-width="180" data-height="35" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Metlife_1970.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Metropolitan Life logo, ca. 1970.</div></div></div>
<p>During the postwar era, the company expanded its suburban presence, decentralized operations, and refocused its career agency system to serve all market segments. It also began to market group insurance products to employers and institutions. By 1979, operations were segmented into four primary businesses: group insurance, personal insurance, pensions, and investments.<sup id="cite_ref-History_38-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History-38">[38]</a></sup> In 1981, MetLife purchased what became known as the MetLife building for $400 million from a group that included <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_World_Airways" title="Pan American World Airways">Pan American World Airways</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PanAm_05_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PanAm_05-39">[39]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BuildingSales_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BuildingSales-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Walter_Gropius_photo_MetLife_Building_fassade_New_York_USA_2005-10-03.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Walter_Gropius_photo_MetLife_Building_fassade_New_York_USA_2005-10-03.jpg/220px-Walter_Gropius_photo_MetLife_Building_fassade_New_York_USA_2005-10-03.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1600"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 293px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Walter_Gropius_photo_MetLife_Building_fassade_New_York_USA_2005-10-03.jpg/220px-Walter_Gropius_photo_MetLife_Building_fassade_New_York_USA_2005-10-03.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="293" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Walter_Gropius_photo_MetLife_Building_fassade_New_York_USA_2005-10-03.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/MetLife_Building" title="MetLife Building">MetLife building</a> at 200 Park Ave in New York City. The building is no longer owned by MetLife</div></div></div>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="De-mutualization_and_IPO">De-mutualization and IPO</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MetLife&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: De-mutualization and IPO" data-section="7" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In 2000, MetLife converted from a mutual insurance company operated for the benefit of its policyholders to a for-profit public company.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The de-mutualization process allowed MetLife to enter unrelated insurance businesses and increase executive compensation.
</p><p>Policyholders received some stock in the new company in this process.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> MetLife was accused of breaching federal securities laws by misrepresenting and omitting information in materials given to policyholders during this process, resulting in years of litigation ending with a $50 million settlement in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:left;"></div>
<h4 class="in-block"><span id="Acquisitions.2C_sales.2C_and_major_deals"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Acquisitions,_sales,_and_major_deals">Acquisitions, sales, and major deals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MetLife&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Acquisitions, sales, and major deals" data-section="8" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<ul><li>1992 - merged with United Mutual Life Insurance Company, the only <a href="/wiki/African-American" class="mw-redirect" title="African-American">African-American</a> life insurer in <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">New York</a>, in 1992.<sup id="cite_ref-Scott93_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scott93-43">[43]</a></sup></li>
<li>1992 - <sup id="cite_ref-Lublin09_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lublin09-44">[44]</a></sup> acquired <a href="/wiki/Executive_Life_Insurance_Company" title="Executive Life Insurance Company">Executive Life</a>'s single premium deferred <a href="/wiki/Annuity_(US_financial_products)" class="mw-redirect" title="Annuity (US financial products)">annuity</a> business, which was worth approximately $1.2 billion. MetLife also acquired the firm's life insurance business, valued at about $260 million.<sup id="cite_ref-Stouffer92_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stouffer92-45">[45]</a></sup></li>
<li>1995 - sold <a href="/wiki/Century_21_(real_estate)" title="Century 21 (real estate)">Century 21</a> to <a href="/wiki/Cendant" title="Cendant">Cendant</a> (known as Hospitality Franchise Systems at the time) while purchasing New England Mutual Life Insurance Company.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></li>
<li>1997 - acquired Security First Group in 1997 for $377 million.<sup id="cite_ref-AP95_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AP95-47">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Garmhausen97_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Garmhausen97-48">[48]</a></sup></li>
<li>1999 - acquired <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_National_Corporation" title="Lincoln National Corporation">Lincoln National Corporation</a>'s individual disability income unit.<sup id="cite_ref-Frazier99_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frazier99-49">[49]</a></sup></li>
<li>1999 - bought out reinsurance provider GenAmerica Corporation for $1.2 billion, as well as its subsidiaries, <a href="/wiki/Reinsurance_Group_of_America" title="Reinsurance Group of America">Reinsurance Group of America</a> and <a href="/wiki/Conning_%26_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Conning &amp; Company">Conning Corporation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Gallagher02_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gallagher02-50">[50]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Moore99_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moore99-51">[51]</a></sup> That year, the company had grown to serve 7 million policyholders.<sup id="cite_ref-Quinn99_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Quinn99-52">[52]</a></sup></li>
<li>2000 - de-mutualization and IPO.<sup id="cite_ref-Vowinkel98_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vowinkel98-53">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Treaster00_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Treaster00-54">[54]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">initial public offering</a> was valued at $6.5 billion, which was the largest IPO to that date in United States financial history.<sup id="cite_ref-Vowinkel98_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vowinkel98-53">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Treaster00_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Treaster00-54">[54]</a></sup> MetLife policyholders were asked to choose a cash or stock stake. This IPO made MetLife the most widely owned stock in the United States, and it raised MetLife's value to over $4 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-Healy99_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Healy99-55">[55]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bridger99_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bridger99-56">[56]</a></sup> By 2000, MetLife's reported number of policyholders had risen to 11 million,<sup id="cite_ref-Bridger99_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bridger99-56">[56]</a></sup> and that year it had become the United States' number one life insurer, surpassing Prudential, according to <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Times00_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Times00-57">[57]</a></sup></li>
<li>2000 - $470 million voice and data network management deal with AT&amp;T Solutions.<sup id="cite_ref-Pappalardo00_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pappalardo00-58">[58]</a></sup></li>
<li>2001 - acquired Grand Bank of <a href="/wiki/Kingston,_New_Jersey" title="Kingston, New Jersey">Kingston, New Jersey</a>, which was renamed MetLife Bank.<sup id="cite_ref-Gjertsen00_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gjertsen00-59">[59]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Jill01_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jill01-60">[60]</a></sup></li>
<li>2001 - invested $1 billion in the United States stock market during 2001, immediately after the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11th terrorist attacks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MetLifeHistory_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MetLifeHistory-61">[61]</a></sup></li>
<li>2005 - acquired <a href="/wiki/Citigroup" title="Citigroup">Citigroup</a>’s Travelers Life &amp; Annuity and all of Citigroup’s international insurance businesses for $11.8 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-Augusturms10_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Augusturms10-62">[62]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ramirez05_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ramirez05-63">[63]</a></sup> At the time of the deal, which was completed on July 1, 2005, the Travelers acquisition made MetLife the largest individual life insurer in North America based on sales.<sup id="cite_ref-Travelers_05_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Travelers_05-64">[64]</a></sup></li>
<li>2006 - opened joint-venture insurance company in <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a>, in May 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-Hongmei06_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hongmei06-65">[65]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Chen07_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chen07-66">[66]</a></sup></li>
<li>2006 - sold <a href="/wiki/Stuyvesant_Town%E2%80%93Peter_Cooper_Village" title="Stuyvesant Town–Peter Cooper Village">Peter Cooper Village, or Stuyvesant Town</a>, the largest apartment complexes in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> at the time, for $5.4 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-Carmiel12_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carmiel12-67">[67]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bagli12_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bagli12-68">[68]</a></sup> MetLife had developed the apartment complexes between 1945 and 1947, to house veterans returning home from serving in <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Henderson14_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Henderson14-69">[69]</a></sup></li>
<li>2010 - bought <a href="/wiki/American_Life_Insurance_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="American Life Insurance Company">American Life Insurance Company</a> from <a href="/wiki/American_International_Group" title="American International Group">AIG</a> for <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>15,500,000,000.<sup id="cite_ref-Augusturms10_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Augusturms10-62">[62]</a></sup></li>
<li>2011 - sold MetLife bank to <a href="/wiki/GE_Capital" title="GE Capital">GE Capital</a>, exiting banking business.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></li></ul><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_era">Current era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MetLife&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Current era" data-section="9" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>From 2004 to 2011, MetLife continued to hold its position as the largest life insurer in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-Frye11_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frye11-71">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lazarus04_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lazarus04-72">[72]</a></sup>  The company had $2.5 trillion in policies written, $350 billion in assets under management, over 12 million customers in the United States, 8 million customers outside the United States, and a net income in 2003 of $2.2 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-Lazarus04_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lazarus04-72">[72]</a></sup> That year, <i><a href="/wiki/Barron%27s_(newspaper)" title="Barron's (newspaper)">Barron's</a></i> reported that 13 million American households owned at least one product from MetLife.<sup id="cite_ref-Lazo04_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lazo04-73">[73]</a></sup></p><p>MetLife named <a href="/wiki/Bob_Benmosche" title="Bob Benmosche">Robert H. Benmosche</a> as chairman and CEO in July 1999. Benmosche occupied the position until 2006, when he was replaced by <a href="/wiki/C._Robert_Henrikson" title="C. Robert Henrikson">C. Robert Henrikson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Frye11_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frye11-71">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hovenisian05_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hovenisian05-74">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IJ05_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IJ05-75">[75]</a></sup></p><p>The company's sales grew 11.5% between 2008 and 2009, despite the <a href="/wiki/Great_Recession_in_the_United_States" title="Great Recession in the United States">national recession</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Galentine10_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Galentine10-76">[76]</a></sup> In 2011, CEO <a href="/wiki/C._Robert_Henrikson" title="C. Robert Henrikson">Robert Henrikson</a> was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Steven_A._Kandarian" title="Steven A. Kandarian">Steven A. Kandarian</a>, who had overseen the company's "<a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>450,000,000,000 investment portfolio" as <a href="/wiki/Chief_investment_officer" title="Chief investment officer">chief investment officer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Frye11_71-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frye11-71">[71]</a></sup>  Henrikson remained the company's chairman to the end of 2011, at which point he reached the company's <a href="/wiki/Mandatory_retirement_age" class="mw-redirect" title="Mandatory retirement age">mandatory retirement age</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Frye11_71-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frye11-71">[71]</a></sup></p><p>In 2015, MetLife was ranked as number one on <i>Fortune</i> magazine's list of World's Most Admired Companies in the Insurance: Life and Health category.<sup id="cite_ref-Fortunelist_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fortunelist-77">[77]</a></sup></p><p>In the summer of 2017, MetLife plans to add a third office building of 255,000 square feet at its <a href="/wiki/Cary,_North_Carolina" title="Cary, North Carolina">Cary, North Carolina</a> Global Technology Campus, giving the company a total of 655,000 square feet at a location which has over 1,000 employees in such areas as engineering, software and technology. This plan was the result of North Carolina awarding the company $94 million in incentives in 2013 for creating over 2,600 jobs, half in Cary and half in <a href="/wiki/Charlotte" class="mw-redirect" title="Charlotte">Charlotte</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id=".22Too_big_to_fail.22"></span><span class="mw-headline" id='"Too_big_to_fail"'>"Too big to fail"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MetLife&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title='Edit section: "Too big to fail"' data-section="10" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2012, MetLife failed the Federal Reserve's (the Fed's) <a href="/wiki/Comprehensive_Capital_Analysis_and_Review" title="Comprehensive Capital Analysis and Review">Comprehensive Capital Analysis and Review</a> stress test, intended to predict the potential failure of the company in a recession. The Fed stated that the minimum total <a href="/wiki/Capital_adequacy_ratio" title="Capital adequacy ratio">risk-based capital ratio</a> should be 8% and it estimated MetLife's ratio at 6%. The company had requested approval for a <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>2,000,000,000 <a href="/wiki/Share_repurchase" title="Share repurchase">share repurchase</a> to prop up the stock price, along with an increased dividend.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> Because MetLife owned MetLife Bank, it was subject to stricter financial regulation. To escape that level of regulation, MetLife announced the sale of its banking unit to <a href="/wiki/GE_Capital" title="GE Capital">GE Capital</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> On November 2, 2012, MetLife said it was selling its <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>70,000,000,000 <a href="/wiki/Mortgage" class="mw-redirect" title="Mortgage">mortgage</a> servicing business to <a href="/wiki/JPMorgan_Chase" title="JPMorgan Chase">JPMorgan Chase</a> for an undisclosed amount.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> Both sales were part of its strategy to focus on the <a href="/wiki/Insurance" title="Insurance">insurance</a> side of its business.
</p><p>The attempt to escape "<a href="/wiki/Too_big_to_fail" title="Too big to fail">too big to fail</a>" regulation was not successful. In September 2014, the United States government observed the <a href="/wiki/Dodd%E2%80%93Frank_Wall_Street_Reform_and_Consumer_Protection_Act" title="Dodd–Frank Wall Street Reform and Consumer Protection Act">2010 Dodd-Frank financial reform law</a> by proposing the application of an official label to MetLife as "<a href="/wiki/Systemically_important_financial_institution" title="Systemically important financial institution">systemically important</a>" to the American economy.<sup id="cite_ref-Garcia15_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Garcia15-83">[83]</a></sup> If implemented, MetLife would be subject to different sets of rules and regulations, with increased oversight from the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Reserve_System" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Reserve System">Federal Reserve</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Garcia15_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Garcia15-83">[83]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dealbook14_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dealbook14-84">[84]</a></sup> The company appealed this proposal in November 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-McGrane15_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McGrane15-85">[85]</a></sup> In December 2014, federal regulators decided that MetLife required the special regulations reserved for financial companies and organizations deemed "systemically important," or "too big to fail".<sup id="cite_ref-Steve14_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steve14-86">[86]</a></sup> MetLife announced in January 2015 that it would file a lawsuit with the <a href="/wiki/United_States_District_Court_for_the_District_of_Columbia" title="United States District Court for the District of Columbia">U.S. District Court for the District of Columbia</a> to overturn the federal regulators' decision,<sup id="cite_ref-Garcia15_83-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Garcia15-83">[83]</a></sup> thus becoming the first nonbank to challenge such a decision.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-87">[87]</a></sup>  Three other nonbank companies have been designated as "systemically important": <a href="/wiki/American_International_Group" title="American International Group">AIG</a>, <a href="/wiki/General_Electric" title="General Electric">General Electric</a> and <a href="/wiki/Prudential_Financial" title="Prudential Financial">Prudential</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Steve14_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steve14-86">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:1_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-87">[87]</a></sup>   MetLife continued to litigate this issue as of mid-2015, with the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Justice" title="United States Department of Justice">US Department of Justice</a> asking that their challenge be dismissed.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_87-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Fines">Fines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MetLife&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Fines" data-section="11" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On August 7, 2012, it was announced that MetLife will pay $3.2 million in fines after the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Reserve" title="Federal Reserve">Federal Reserve</a> charged it used unsafe and unsound practices in handling its mortgage servicing and foreclosure operations.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p><p>In 2014, MetLife paid $23 million to settle multiple lawsuits over <a href="/wiki/Junk_fax" title="Junk fax">junk fax</a> operations used to generate leads for life insurance sales.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style=";"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r887775652">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%;max-width:100%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{margin:0.5em auto 0.8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft p,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright p{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:larger;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" “ ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" ” ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:360px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{min-width:100%;margin:0 0 0.8em!important;float:none!important}}</style><div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">"MetLife Bank took advantage of the FHA insurance program by knowingly turning a blind eye to mortgage loans that did not meet basic underwriting requirements, and stuck the FHA and taxpayers with the bill when those mortgages defaulted."</div>
<p><cite class="left-aligned" style=""><i>U.S. Attorney John Walsh</i></cite>
</p>
</div>
<p>In 2015, MetLife Home Loans LLC paid $123.5 million to the United States Department of Justice to resolve allegations it knowingly made mortgages insured by the United States government that didn't meet federal underwriting requirements.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(3)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Products_and_services">Products and services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MetLife&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Products and services" data-section="12" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-3 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-3">

of Records, Yonkers, New York.</div></div></div>
<p>As of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=MetLife&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, MetLife had a "diverse product mix" which included insurance (<a href="/wiki/Home_insurance" title="Home insurance">home</a>, <a href="/wiki/Car_insurance" class="mw-redirect" title="Car insurance">car</a> and <a href="/wiki/Life_insurance" title="Life insurance">life</a>), <a href="/wiki/Variable_annuity" class="mw-redirect" title="Variable annuity">variable life annuities</a> and <a href="/wiki/Structured_Settlements" class="mw-redirect" title="Structured Settlements">structured settlements</a>, <a href="/wiki/Commercial_mortgages" class="mw-redirect" title="Commercial mortgages">commercial mortgages</a> and <a href="/wiki/Commercial_mortgage-backed_security" title="Commercial mortgage-backed security">securities backed by commercial mortgages</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_debt" class="mw-redirect" title="Sovereign debt">sovereign debt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MexEng_103_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MexEng_103-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Life_insurance">Life insurance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MetLife&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Life insurance" data-section="13" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>MetLife's individual <a href="/wiki/Life_insurance" title="Life insurance">life insurance</a> products and services comprise <a href="/wiki/Term_life_insurance" title="Term life insurance">term life insurance</a> and several types of <a href="/wiki/Permanent_life_insurance" class="mw-redirect" title="Permanent life insurance">permanent life insurance</a>, including whole life, universal life, and final expense whole life insurance.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> These services vary in regards to the duration and amount of coverage available and whether a medical exam is required for coverage. The company also offers group life insurance, provided through employers, which consists of term life, permanent life, and accidental death and dismemberment coverage.<sup id="cite_ref-InsuranceProducts_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-InsuranceProducts-93">[93]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GroupInsuranceProducts_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GroupInsuranceProducts-94">[94]</a></sup> MetLife is the largest life insurer in the United States, based on life insurance in-force.<sup id="cite_ref-Ninety_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ninety-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MexEng_103_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MexEng_103-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Dental">Dental</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MetLife&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Dental" data-section="14" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>MetLife offers group dental benefit plans for individuals, employees, retirees and their families and provides dental plan administration for over 20 million people.<sup id="cite_ref-TwentyMillionDental_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TwentyMillionDental-95">[95]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DentalCoverage_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DentalCoverage-96">[96]</a></sup> Plans include MetLife's Preferred Dentist Program (PPO) and the SafeGuard DHMO (available for both individuals and employees in CA, FL, TX, NJ and NY.). As of May 2010, MetLife's dental <a href="/wiki/Preferred_provider_organization" title="Preferred provider organization">PPO</a> network included over 135,000 participating dentist locations nationwide while the dental <a href="/wiki/HMO" class="mw-redirect" title="HMO">HMO</a> network included more than 13,000 participating dentist locations in <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a> and <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Dental_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dental-97">[97]</a></sup> MetLife also administers dental continuing education program for dentists and allied health care professionals, which are recognized by the <a href="/wiki/American_Dental_Association" title="American Dental Association">American Dental Association</a> (ADA) and the <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_General_Dentistry" title="Academy of General Dentistry">Academy of General Dentistry</a> (AGD).<sup id="cite_ref-ADA_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ADA-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Disability">Disability</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MetLife&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Disability" data-section="15" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>MetLife provides disability products for individuals as well as employee and association groups who receive them through their employer.<sup id="cite_ref-Disability10K_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Disability10K-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> For individuals, the company's individual disability income insurance can replace a portion of lost income if an individual is unable to work due to sickness or injury.<sup id="cite_ref-DisabilityInsurance_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DisabilityInsurance-100">[100]</a></sup> MetLife offers several individual disability income policies, including MetLife Income Guard, OMNI Advantage, OMNI Essential, Business Overhead Expense, and Buy-Sell.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> The policy options provided by the company vary in terms of eligibility and the provided coverage. For groups, MetLife offers short term <a href="/wiki/Disability_insurance" title="Disability insurance">disability insurance</a> and long term disability insurance.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> Short term disability insurance is structured to replace a portion of an individual's income during the initial weeks of a disabling illness or accident.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> Long term disability Insurance serves to replace a portion of an individual's income during an extended period of a disabling <a href="/wiki/Illness" class="mw-redirect" title="Illness">illness</a> or <a href="/wiki/Accident" title="Accident">accident</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DisabilityInsuranceProducts_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DisabilityInsuranceProducts-104">[104]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> The company also maintains an absence management product which allows employers to track and manage both planned and unplanned employee absences. The product, which MetLife calls MetLife Total Absence Management, is structured for businesses with 1,000 or more employees.<sup id="cite_ref-TotalAbsence_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TotalAbsence-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Annuities">Annuities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MetLife&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Annuities" data-section="16" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>MetLife is among the largest providers of <a href="/wiki/Annuity_(US_financial_products)" class="mw-redirect" title="Annuity (US financial products)">annuities</a> in the world, recording $22.4 billion in sales during 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-Numberoneann_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Numberoneann-107">[107]</a></sup> MetLife offers annuities which consist of fixed annuities, variable annuities, deferred annuities and immediate annuities.<sup id="cite_ref-AnnuitiesProducts_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AnnuitiesProducts-108">[108]</a></sup> In 1921, MetLife was the first company to issue a group annuity contract.<sup id="cite_ref-FirstAnnuity_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FirstAnnuity-109">[109]</a></sup> More recently in 2004, it was the first insurer to introduce a longevity insurance product.<sup id="cite_ref-LongevityInsurance_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LongevityInsurance-110">[110]</a></sup> As of December 31, 2009, MetLife globally managed group annuity assets of $60 billion with $34 billion of transferred pension liabilities and provided benefit payments to over 600,000 annuitants per month.<sup id="cite_ref-AnnuityInformation_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AnnuityInformation-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Auto_.26_Home"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Auto_&amp;_Home">Auto &amp; Home</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MetLife&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Auto &amp; Home" data-section="17" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>MetLife Auto &amp; Home is the brand name for MetLife's nine affiliate personal lines insurance companies.<sup id="cite_ref-AutoHomeBrand_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoHomeBrand-112">[112]</a></sup> Collectively these companies offer personal lines property and casualty insurance policies in all 50 states and the District of Columbia.<sup id="cite_ref-PRN_05_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PRN_05-113">[113]</a></sup> The flagship company in the MetLife Auto &amp; Home group, Metropolitan Property and Casualty Insurance Company, was founded in 1972.<sup id="cite_ref-AutoHomeBrand_112-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoHomeBrand-112">[112]</a></sup> MetLife Auto &amp; Home companies presently have over 2.7 million active policies and service 58 of the Fortune 100 companies.<sup id="cite_ref-Teens_10_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Teens_10-114">[114]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FortuneEBN_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FortuneEBN-115">[115]</a></sup></p><p>MetLife's home insurance includes homeowners insurance, condo insurance, <a href="/wiki/Renters%27_insurance" title="Renters' insurance">renters insurance</a>, insurance for landlords, and mobile home insurance.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> The available policies for MetLife's home insurance provide coverage for possessions, property damage from natural disaster or theft, and various legal expenses incurred resulting from injuries sustained on an individual's property.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> The companies also sell RV, ATV, boat, mobile home, collectible vehicle, and motorcycle policies<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> and offers flood insurance policies as a participant in the National Flood Insurance Program (NFIP), which is managed by the federal government.<sup id="cite_ref-Flood_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flood-120">[120]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NFIP_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NFIP-121">[121]</a></sup> MetLife's various types of coverage for auto insurance include liability protection, collision and comprehensive coverage, personal injury protection, rental car coverage, and uninsured and underinsured motorists coverage.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> Through an arrangement with Hyatt Legal Plans, a subsidiary of MetLife, MetLife Auto &amp; Home underwrites group legal plans in many states.<sup id="cite_ref-HyattLegal_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HyattLegal-19">[19]</a></sup></p><p>It was the first national insurer in the United States to offer identity-theft resolution services at no extra premium and as of 2012 continues to do so today in most United States states.<sup id="cite_ref-IDTheft_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IDTheft-124">[124]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ContinCoverage_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ContinCoverage-125">[125]</a></sup> In 2010, MetLife Auto &amp; Home began offering their GrandProtect plan in most states. This GrandProtect policy simplifies complex insurance needs by combining a client's home, valuable items, autos, RVs, and boats into one comprehensive policy package. The ultimate benefits to the consumer are having one bill, only one deductible, comprehensive coverage, and typically lower rates than trying to get each policy individually.<sup id="cite_ref-GrandProtect_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GrandProtect-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_products">Other products</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MetLife&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Other products" data-section="18" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>MetLife's products also include <a href="/wiki/Critical_illness_insurance" title="Critical illness insurance">critical illness insurance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Criticalillness_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Criticalillness-127">[127]</a></sup> Financial services include fee-based financial planning, retirement planning, wealth management, 529 Plans, banking, and commercial and residential <a href="/wiki/Mortgages" class="mw-redirect" title="Mortgages">mortgages</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Other_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Other-128">[128]</a></sup> The company also provides retirement plan and other financial services to healthcare, education, and not-for-profit organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-NonProfitRetirement_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NonProfitRetirement-129">[129]</a></sup> The MetLife Center for Special Needs Planning is a group of planners which serve families and individuals with special needs.<sup id="cite_ref-SpecialNeeds_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SpecialNeeds-130">[130]</a></sup> In 2014, MetLife launched MetLife Defender, a digital <a href="/wiki/Identity_theft" title="Identity theft">identity theft</a> protection product.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(4)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="International_presence">International presence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MetLife&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: International presence" data-section="19" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-4 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-4">
<p>Outside of the United States, MetLife operates in Latin America, Europe, Asia's Pacific region, and the Middle East, with leading market positions in Mexico, Japan, South Korea and Chile.<sup id="cite_ref-AlicoInternational_10_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AlicoInternational_10-9">[9]</a></sup></p><p>On March 8, 2010, MetLife announced its intent to purchase the international leader life-insurance business, American Life Insurance Company (Alico), from <a href="/wiki/American_International_Group" title="American International Group">American International Group</a> (AIG). MetLife, which completed the deal on November 1, 2010, paid approximately $7.2 billion in cash and $9.0 billion in MetLife equity and other securities.<sup id="cite_ref-SalePrice_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SalePrice-132">[132]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GlobalWall_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GlobalWall-133">[133]</a></sup> The securities portion of the deal consisted of 78.2 million shares of MetLife common stock, 6.9 million shares of contingent convertible preferred stock and 40 million equity units.<sup id="cite_ref-ALICOSTATS_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ALICOSTATS-134">[134]</a></sup> The values of the common and preferred stock were based on the closing price of MetLife's common stock on October 29.<sup id="cite_ref-ALICOSTATS_134-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ALICOSTATS-134">[134]</a></sup>  Upon completion of the purchase, MetLife became a leading competitor in <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, the world's second-largest life insurance market, and moved into a top 5 market position in many high growth emerging markets in <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Middle_East" class="mw-redirect" title="The Middle East">the Middle East</a> and <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ALICOSTATS_134-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ALICOSTATS-134">[134]</a></sup> The deal added 20 million customers to MetLife's 70 million and according to <i>Barron's</i> more than doubled the percentage of operating profits that MetLife gets abroad to 40%.<sup id="cite_ref-MexEng_103_15-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MexEng_103-15">[15]</a></sup></p><p>In India MetLife has an affiliate company <i>India Insurance Company Limited (MetLife)</i> which has operated in India since 2001.  This company has its headquarters in Bangalore and Gurgaon and was jointly owned by MetLife and a few local Indian financial companies.  In 2012 an agreement was made with local Indian bank, the <a href="/wiki/Punjab_National_Bank" title="Punjab National Bank">Punjab National Bank</a> to establish a strategic alliance and for it to take a 30% share in MetLife India.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup>  The state owned bank would in return sell MetLife insurance products in its branches
</p><p>As of 2015, Julio Garcia-Villalon leads the Middle East &amp; Africa regional business, which is headquartered in the <a href="/wiki/Dubai_International_Financial_Centre" title="Dubai International Financial Centre">Dubai International Financial Centre</a> and has operated in the region since the 1950s.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(5)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="MetLife_Foundation">MetLife Foundation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MetLife&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: MetLife Foundation" data-section="20" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-5 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-5">
<p>MetLife Foundation is MetLife's independent charitable and <a href="/wiki/Grant_(money)" title="Grant (money)">grant-awarding</a> <a href="/wiki/Foundation_(nonprofit)" title="Foundation (nonprofit)">foundation</a>. It was founded in 1976<sup id="cite_ref-Peralta15_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peralta15-137">[137]</a></sup> and had provided over $650 million in grants by January 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-Peralta15_137-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peralta15-137">[137]</a></sup> The foundation has partnered with and donated to a variety of organizations, including <a href="/wiki/Habitat_for_Humanity" title="Habitat for Humanity">Habitat for Humanity</a> since 2010<sup id="cite_ref-Amedro08_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Amedro08-138">[138]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther_King,_Jr._Memorial" class="mw-redirect" title="Martin Luther King, Jr. Memorial">Martin Luther King, Jr. National Memorial Project Foundation</a> since 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-Curry11_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Curry11-139">[139]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Memorial08_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Memorial08-140">[140]</a></sup> In 2013, the MetLife Foundation announced a new focus on <a href="/wiki/Financial_inclusion" title="Financial inclusion">financial inclusion</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-MFFI_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MFFI-141">[141]</a></sup> including educational programs on basic financial planning for disadvantaged children<sup id="cite_ref-Kashmir14_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kashmir14-142">[142]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ECT15_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECT15-143">[143]</a></sup> and financial services aimed at low-income communities.<sup id="cite_ref-ECT15_143-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECT15-143">[143]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Moses15_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moses15-144">[144]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Cook15_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cook15-145">[145]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(6)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Relationship_with_Peanuts">Relationship with <i>Peanuts</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MetLife&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Relationship with Peanuts" data-section="21" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-6 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-6">
<p>MetLife's use of comic strip characters, according to <a href="/wiki/Chief_marketing_officer" title="Chief marketing officer">chief marketing officer</a> Esther Lee, was intended "to make our company more friendly and approachable during a time when insurance companies were seen as cold and distant."<sup id="cite_ref-retools_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-retools-146">[146]</a></sup></p><p>MetLife licensed <a href="/wiki/Snoopy" title="Snoopy">Snoopy</a> and other <i><a href="/wiki/Peanuts" title="Peanuts">Peanuts</a></i> characters for promotional purposes from the <a href="/wiki/Iconix_Brand_Group" title="Iconix Brand Group">Iconix Brand Group</a>, which owns the promotional rights to the works of <a href="/wiki/Charles_M._Schulz" title="Charles M. Schulz">Charles M. Schulz</a>. In 2010, Iconix formed a joint venture with Schulz's heirs (as Charles Schulz himself died in 2000), buying out <a href="/wiki/E._W._Scripps" title="E. W. Scripps">E. W. Scripps</a> Co. and <a href="/wiki/United_Features_Syndicate" class="mw-redirect" title="United Features Syndicate">United Features Syndicate</a> for $175 million. MetLife is reported to pay $12 million per year to Iconix for licensing rights.<sup id="cite_ref-forbescb_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbescb-147">[147]</a></sup> Prior to the Iconix deal, MetLife had licensed the characters from other rights-holders.
</p><p>The Peanuts-based campaign was developed by the advertising agency <a href="/wiki/Young_%26_Rubicam" title="Young &amp; Rubicam">Young &amp; Rubicam</a>.  MetLife also has used <a href="/wiki/Foote_Cone_%26_Belding" class="mw-redirect" title="Foote Cone &amp; Belding">Foote Cone &amp; Belding</a> to develop Peanuts-related promotions.<sup id="cite_ref-Campaign1_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Campaign1-148">[148]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Campaign2_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Campaign2-149">[149]</a></sup></p><p>MetLife announced the end of its 31-year relationship with <i><a href="/wiki/Peanuts" title="Peanuts">Peanuts</a></i> on October 20, 2016. This decision resulted from the company's sale of its life insurance business to concentrate on corporate clients.<sup id="cite_ref-retools_146-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-retools-146">[146]</a></sup> MetLife's new blue and green logo was criticized for being a knock-off of comparison website Diffen.<sup id="cite_ref-campaignus_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-campaignus-150">[150]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nypostlogo_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nypostlogo-151">[151]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(7)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Blimp_and_sports_sponsorship">Blimp and sports sponsorship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MetLife&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Blimp and sports sponsorship" data-section="22" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-7 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-7">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Metlife_snoopy_two_blimp.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Metlife_snoopy_two_blimp.jpg/220px-Metlife_snoopy_two_blimp.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1333"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 147px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Metlife_snoopy_two_blimp.jpg/220px-Metlife_snoopy_two_blimp.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="147" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Metlife_snoopy_two_blimp.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Metlife 'Snoopy Two' blimp.</div></div></div>
<p>The MetLife blimp program began in 1987 with the “Snoopy 1” airship and, in 1994, expanded to include the “Snoopy 2” airship.<sup id="cite_ref-BlimpsOrigin_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BlimpsOrigin-152">[152]</a></sup> The program provides aerial coverage to over 80 major sporting events every year and is currently the official aerial coverage provider of the PGA Tour.<sup id="cite_ref-PGATour_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PGATour-153">[153]</a></sup> “Snoopy 1” and “Snoopy 2” also provide overhead television coverage for the <a href="/wiki/NFL" class="mw-redirect" title="NFL">NFL</a>, <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a> College Football, the <a href="/wiki/LPGA" title="LPGA">LPGA</a>, the <a href="/wiki/NBA_Finals" title="NBA Finals">NBA Finals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copa_Chile" title="Copa Chile">Copa Chile</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Preakness_Stakes" title="Preakness Stakes">Preakness Stakes</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Kentucky_Derby" title="Kentucky Derby">Kentucky Derby</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PGATour_153-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PGATour-153">[153]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Horses_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Horses-154">[154]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SportingLife_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SportingLife-155">[155]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CBSFootball_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CBSFootball-156">[156]</a></sup> On August 23, 2011, MetLife agreed to a 25-year sponsorship deal to rename New Meadowlands Stadium in <a href="/wiki/East_Rutherford,_New_Jersey" title="East Rutherford, New Jersey">East Rutherford, New Jersey</a>, home of the NFL's <a href="/wiki/New_York_Giants" title="New York Giants">New York Giants</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_York_Jets" title="New York Jets">New York Jets</a> to <a href="/wiki/MetLife_Stadium" title="MetLife Stadium">MetLife Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup>  On January 16, 2017, MetLife agreed to a five-year sponsorship to rename Seibu Dome in <a href="/wiki/Tokorozawa,_Saitama" title="Tokorozawa, Saitama">Tokorozawa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saitama_Prefecture" title="Saitama Prefecture">Saitama Prefecture</a> in Japan as the <a href="/wiki/MetLife_Dome" title="MetLife Dome">MetLife Dome</a>.
</p><p>From 2014 to 2017, MetLife is the title sponsor of the <a href="/wiki/BWF_Super_Series" title="BWF Super Series">BWF Super Series</a> badminton tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(8)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span id="MetLife_and_the_.E2.80.9CIdeal_weight.E2.80.9D"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="MetLife_and_the_“Ideal_weight”">MetLife and the “Ideal weight”</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MetLife&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: MetLife and the “Ideal weight”" data-section="23" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-8 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-8">
<p>In 1959, The Metropolitan Life Insurance Company (as it was known at the time) released tables of the best weight for each height for longevity, based on their collected insurance data. These tables showed the “desirable weights”. In 1983, they released tables showing the “ideal” weights for greatest longevity; this information was based on data collected in the Build Study of 1979 collected by the <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Actuaries" title="Society of Actuaries">Society of Actuaries</a>. This data followed patients for 18 years (from 1954-1972) and was collected from 25 life insurance companies in Canada and the United States, representing 4.2 million people. These “ideal” weights were higher than the prior “desirable” weights, this was attributed to an increase in muscle mass due to improved fitness levels among the population. This study is still the largest available pool of data for this purpose. It was noticed that the average weights in the population are higher than the ideal weights for survival. The ‘’’Metropolitan Tables’’’ included ‘’small’’, ‘’medium’’ and ‘’large’’ frames, based on elbow-girth measured using calipers, as the elbows do not develop adipose tissue. They presented weight ranges for height, sex and body frame (again associated with the lowest mortality) The midpoint of the ideal weight for the medium frames for each height was selected as the “ideal” weight used for calculations of “excess weight” (initial weight minus ideal weight). This led to a formula to calculate the ideal weight used by <a href="/wiki/Bariatrics" title="Bariatrics">bariatric</a> surgeons, but it had lost considerable accuracy by 2007, again due to improvements in medical care and in public health.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(9)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=MetLife&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: See also" data-section="24" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-9 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-9">
